"""Paged attention decode kernel implemented in Triton.

Conforms to the same Model/get_inputs/get_init_inputs interface as reference.py.
"""
import math

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import triton
import triton.language as tl


OP_TYPE = "attention"
SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]

BATCH = 8
NUM_HEADS = 32
NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
HEAD_DIM = 128
SEQ_LEN = 1024
PAGE_SIZE = 16


@triton.jit
def paged_decode_kernel(
    q_ptr,
    kv_ptr,
    block_table_ptr,
    seq_lens_ptr,
    out_ptr,
    stride_qb,
    stride_qh,
    stride_qd,
    stride_kvn,
    stride_kvt,
    stride_kvh,
    stride_kvd,
    stride_bt_b,
    stride_bt_p,
    stride_ob,
    stride_oh,
    stride_od,
    SCALE: tl.constexpr,
    PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
    G: tl.constexpr,
):
    """One CUDA block per (batch, kv_head). Computes all G query heads."""
    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
    pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1)

    seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens_ptr + pid_b)
    num_pages = tl.cdiv(seq_len, PAGE_SIZE)

    offs_d = tl.arange(0, HEAD_DIM)
    offs_t = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)
    offs_g = tl.arange(0, G)[:, None]
    offs_g1 = tl.arange(0, G)

    # Load the G query heads for this KV group: (G, HEAD_DIM).
    q_ptrs = (
        q_ptr
        + pid_b * stride_qb
        + (pid_hkv * G + offs_g) * stride_qh
        + offs_d[None, :] * stride_qd
    )
    qs = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)

    ms = tl.full((G,), float("-inf"), dtype=tl.float32)
    ls = tl.zeros((G,), dtype=tl.float32)
    accs = tl.zeros((G, HEAD_DIM), dtype=tl.float32)

    for p in range(num_pages):
        physical_block = tl.load(
            block_table_ptr + pid_b * stride_bt_b + p * stride_bt_p
        ).to(tl.int64)
        token_offset = p * PAGE_SIZE
        valid = tl.minimum(PAGE_SIZE, seq_len - token_offset)

        kv_base = kv_ptr + physical_block * stride_kvn + pid_hkv * stride_kvh
        k_ptrs = kv_base + (offs_t[:, None] * stride_kvt + offs_d[None, :] * stride_kvd)
        k = tl.load(
            k_ptrs,
            mask=(offs_t[:, None] < valid) & (offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM),
            other=0.0,
        ).to(tl.float32)
        v_ptrs = kv_base + HEAD_DIM * stride_kvd + (
            offs_t[:, None] * stride_kvt + offs_d[None, :] * stride_kvd
        )
        v = tl.load(
            v_ptrs,
            mask=(offs_t[:, None] < valid) & (offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM),
            other=0.0,
        ).to(tl.float32)

        for g in tl.static_range(G):
            mask_g = tl.arange(0, G) == g
            mask_g2 = mask_g[:, None]
            q = tl.sum(tl.where(mask_g2, qs, 0.0), axis=0)
            acc_cur = tl.sum(tl.where(mask_g2, accs, 0.0), axis=0)
            m_cur = tl.sum(tl.where(mask_g, ms, 0.0), axis=0)
            l_cur = tl.sum(tl.where(mask_g, ls, 0.0), axis=0)

            scores = tl.reshape(tl.dot(q[None, :], tl.trans(k)), (PAGE_SIZE,)) * SCALE
            scores = tl.where(offs_t < valid, scores, float("-inf"))

            m_new = tl.maximum(m_cur, tl.max(scores, axis=0))
            exp_scale = tl.exp(m_cur - m_new)
            exp_scores = tl.exp(scores - m_new)
            weighted = tl.reshape(tl.dot(exp_scores[None, :], v), (HEAD_DIM,))

            new_acc = acc_cur * exp_scale + weighted
            new_l = l_cur * exp_scale + tl.sum(exp_scores, axis=0)

            accs = tl.where(mask_g2, new_acc[None, :], accs)
            ls = tl.where(mask_g, new_l, ls)
            ms = tl.where(mask_g, m_new, ms)

    out_ptrs = (
        out_ptr
        + pid_b * stride_ob
        + (pid_hkv * G + offs_g) * stride_oh
        + offs_d[None, :] * stride_od
    )
    tl.store(
        out_ptrs,
        (accs / ls[:, None]).to(tl.bfloat16),
        mask=offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM,
    )


@triton.jit
def paged_decode_part_kernel(
    q_ptr,
    kv_ptr,
    block_table_ptr,
    seq_lens_ptr,
    part_out_ptr,
    part_m_ptr,
    part_l_ptr,
    stride_qb,
    stride_qh,
    stride_qd,
    stride_kvn,
    stride_kvt,
    stride_kvh,
    stride_kvd,
    stride_bt_b,
    stride_bt_p,
    stride_pob,
    stride_poh,
    stride_pos,
    stride_pod,
    stride_pmb,
    stride_pmh,
    stride_pms,
    SCALE: tl.constexpr,
    PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
    G: tl.constexpr,
    NUM_SPLITS: tl.constexpr,
):
    """One CUDA block per (batch, kv_head, split). Computes partial attention."""
    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
    pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1)
    pid_s = tl.program_id(2)

    seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens_ptr + pid_b)
    num_pages = tl.cdiv(seq_len, PAGE_SIZE)
    pages_per_split = tl.cdiv(num_pages, NUM_SPLITS)
    start_page = pid_s * pages_per_split
    end_page = tl.minimum(num_pages, start_page + pages_per_split)

    offs_d = tl.arange(0, HEAD_DIM)
    offs_t = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)
    offs_g = tl.arange(0, G)[:, None]
    offs_g1 = tl.arange(0, G)

    # Load the G query heads for this KV group: (G, HEAD_DIM).
    q_ptrs = (
        q_ptr
        + pid_b * stride_qb
        + (pid_hkv * G + offs_g) * stride_qh
        + offs_d[None, :] * stride_qd
    )
    qs = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)

    ms = tl.full((G,), float("-inf"), dtype=tl.float32)
    ls = tl.zeros((G,), dtype=tl.float32)
    accs = tl.zeros((G, HEAD_DIM), dtype=tl.float32)

    for p in range(start_page, end_page):
        physical_block = tl.load(
            block_table_ptr + pid_b * stride_bt_b + p * stride_bt_p
        ).to(tl.int64)
        token_offset = p * PAGE_SIZE
        valid = tl.minimum(PAGE_SIZE, seq_len - token_offset)

        kv_base = kv_ptr + physical_block * stride_kvn + pid_hkv * stride_kvh
        k_ptrs = kv_base + (offs_t[:, None] * stride_kvt + offs_d[None, :] * stride_kvd)
        k = tl.load(
            k_ptrs,
            mask=(offs_t[:, None] < valid) & (offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM),
            other=0.0,
        ).to(tl.float32)
        v_ptrs = kv_base + HEAD_DIM * stride_kvd + (
            offs_t[:, None] * stride_kvt + offs_d[None, :] * stride_kvd
        )
        v = tl.load(
            v_ptrs,
            mask=(offs_t[:, None] < valid) & (offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM),
            other=0.0,
        ).to(tl.float32)

        for g in tl.static_range(G):
            mask_g = tl.arange(0, G) == g
            mask_g2 = mask_g[:, None]
            q = tl.sum(tl.where(mask_g2, qs, 0.0), axis=0)
            acc_cur = tl.sum(tl.where(mask_g2, accs, 0.0), axis=0)
            m_cur = tl.sum(tl.where(mask_g, ms, 0.0), axis=0)
            l_cur = tl.sum(tl.where(mask_g, ls, 0.0), axis=0)

            scores = tl.reshape(tl.dot(q[None, :], tl.trans(k)), (PAGE_SIZE,)) * SCALE
            scores = tl.where(offs_t < valid, scores, float("-inf"))

            m_new = tl.maximum(m_cur, tl.max(scores, axis=0))
            exp_scale = tl.exp(m_cur - m_new)
            exp_scores = tl.exp(scores - m_new)
            weighted = tl.reshape(tl.dot(exp_scores[None, :], v), (HEAD_DIM,))

            new_acc = acc_cur * exp_scale + weighted
            new_l = l_cur * exp_scale + tl.sum(exp_scores, axis=0)

            accs = tl.where(mask_g2, new_acc[None, :], accs)
            ls = tl.where(mask_g, new_l, ls)
            ms = tl.where(mask_g, m_new, ms)

    # Write partials for all G query heads in the group at once.
    out_ptrs = (
        part_out_ptr
        + pid_b * stride_pob
        + (pid_hkv * G + offs_g) * stride_poh
        + pid_s * stride_pos
        + offs_d[None, :] * stride_pod
    )
    tl.store(out_ptrs, accs, mask=offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM)
    m_ptrs = (
        part_m_ptr
        + pid_b * stride_pmb
        + (pid_hkv * G + offs_g1) * stride_pmh
        + pid_s * stride_pms
    )
    tl.store(m_ptrs, ms)
    l_ptrs = (
        part_l_ptr
        + pid_b * stride_pmb
        + (pid_hkv * G + offs_g1) * stride_pmh
        + pid_s * stride_pms
    )
    tl.store(l_ptrs, ls)


@triton.jit
def combine_kernel(
    part_out_ptr,
    part_m_ptr,
    part_l_ptr,
    out_ptr,
    stride_pob,
    stride_poh,
    stride_pos,
    stride_pod,
    stride_pmb,
    stride_pmh,
    stride_pms,
    stride_ob,
    stride_oh,
    stride_od,
    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
    NUM_SPLITS: tl.constexpr,
):
    """Combine partial attention results across splits."""
    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
    pid_h = tl.program_id(1)

    offs_d = tl.arange(0, HEAD_DIM)

    M = tl.full((), float("-inf"), dtype=tl.float32)
    denom = tl.zeros((), dtype=tl.float32)
    acc = tl.zeros((HEAD_DIM,), dtype=tl.float32)

    base_out = part_out_ptr + pid_b * stride_pob + pid_h * stride_poh
    base_m = part_m_ptr + pid_b * stride_pmb + pid_h * stride_pmh
    base_l = part_l_ptr + pid_b * stride_pmb + pid_h * stride_pmh

    for s in tl.static_range(NUM_SPLITS):
        m_s = tl.load(base_m + s * stride_pms)
        l_s = tl.load(base_l + s * stride_pms)
        acc_s = tl.load(base_out + s * stride_pos + offs_d * stride_pod, mask=offs_d < HEAD_DIM, other=0.0)

        M_new = tl.maximum(M, m_s)
        scale_global = tl.exp(M - M_new)
        scale_s = tl.exp(m_s - M_new)

        acc = acc * scale_global + acc_s * scale_s
        denom = denom * scale_global + l_s * scale_s
        M = M_new

    out_ptrs = out_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob + pid_h * stride_oh + offs_d * stride_od
    tl.store(
        out_ptrs,
        (acc / denom).to(tl.bfloat16),
        mask=offs_d < HEAD_DIM,
    )


class Model(nn.Module):
    def __init__(
        self,
        batch: int,
        num_heads: int,
        num_kv_heads: int,
        head_dim: int,
        seq_len: int,
        page_size: int,
    ):
        super().__init__()
        assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0, "num_heads must be a multiple of num_kv_heads (GQA)"
        self.batch = batch
        self.num_heads = num_heads
        self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads
        self.head_dim = head_dim
        self.seq_len = seq_len
        self.page_size = page_size
        self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads
        self.scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)

        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False)

    def forward(
        self,
        query: torch.Tensor,
        kv_cache: torch.Tensor,
        block_table: torch.Tensor,
        seq_lens: torch.Tensor,
    ) -> torch.Tensor:
        B, H, D = query.shape
        Hkv = self.num_kv_heads
        G = self.group_size
        P = self.page_size
        device = query.device

        out = torch.empty(B, H, D, dtype=query.dtype, device=device)

        # Use sequence splitting when there are too few (batch, kv_head) tiles to
        # keep the GPU busy. Aim for ~256 active blocks.
        blocks = B * Hkv
        num_splits = max(1, 256 // blocks)
        max_pages = (int(seq_lens.max().item()) + P - 1) // P
        num_splits = min(num_splits, max_pages)

        if num_splits == 1:
            grid = (B, Hkv)
            paged_decode_kernel[grid](
                query,
                kv_cache,
                block_table,
                seq_lens,
                out,
                query.stride(0),
                query.stride(1),
                query.stride(2),
                kv_cache.stride(0),
                kv_cache.stride(1),
                kv_cache.stride(2),
                kv_cache.stride(3),
                block_table.stride(0),
                block_table.stride(1),
                out.stride(0),
                out.stride(1),
                out.stride(2),
                SCALE=self.scale,
                PAGE_SIZE=P,
                HEAD_DIM=D,
                G=G,
                num_warps=4,
            )
            return out

        part_out = torch.empty(B, H, num_splits, D, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
        part_m = torch.empty(B, H, num_splits, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
        part_l = torch.empty(B, H, num_splits, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)

        grid_part = (B, Hkv, num_splits)
        paged_decode_part_kernel[grid_part](
            query,
            kv_cache,
            block_table,
            seq_lens,
            part_out,
            part_m,
            part_l,
            query.stride(0),
            query.stride(1),
            query.stride(2),
            kv_cache.stride(0),
            kv_cache.stride(1),
            kv_cache.stride(2),
            kv_cache.stride(3),
            block_table.stride(0),
            block_table.stride(1),
            part_out.stride(0),
            part_out.stride(1),
            part_out.stride(2),
            part_out.stride(3),
            part_m.stride(0),
            part_m.stride(1),
            part_m.stride(2),
            SCALE=self.scale,
            PAGE_SIZE=P,
            HEAD_DIM=D,
            G=G,
            NUM_SPLITS=num_splits,
            num_warps=4,
        )

        grid_combine = (B, H)
        combine_kernel[grid_combine](
            part_out,
            part_m,
            part_l,
            out,
            part_out.stride(0),
            part_out.stride(1),
            part_out.stride(2),
            part_out.stride(3),
            part_m.stride(0),
            part_m.stride(1),
            part_m.stride(2),
            out.stride(0),
            out.stride(1),
            out.stride(2),
            HEAD_DIM=D,
            NUM_SPLITS=num_splits,
            num_warps=2,
        )

        return out


def get_inputs():
    B = BATCH
    H = NUM_HEADS
    Hkv = NUM_KV_HEADS
    D = HEAD_DIM
    L = SEQ_LEN
    P = PAGE_SIZE

    pages_per_seq = (L + P - 1) // P
    total_pages = max(B * pages_per_seq + 8, 64)

    query = torch.randn(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    kv_cache = torch.randn(total_pages, P, Hkv, 2 * D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1

    perm = torch.randperm(total_pages)[: B * pages_per_seq].reshape(B, pages_per_seq).int()
    block_table = perm.contiguous()
    seq_lens = torch.full((B,), L, dtype=torch.int32)

    return [query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [BATCH, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM, SEQ_LEN, PAGE_SIZE]
Implemented the paged-attention decode kernel in `solution.py`. What it does: - Custom Triton kernel (no forbidden ops / libraries). - One CUDA block per `(batch, kv_head)` so the KV cache is streamed only once per KV head; each block computes all GQA query heads in the group. - Fused online softmax in fp32, with predicated masking for non-power-of-two sequence lengths. - Splits the page sequence into partitions when batch × kv-head is small, then combines partial softmax states in a second small kernel. This boosts occupancy on the long-context / small-batch shapes. - Uses `tl.dot` for the QK and PV reductions on each page tile. Verification: - `python check.py` → **PASS** across all five shapes and seeds. - `python benchmark.py` → **RESULT: OK** with a geometric-mean peak fraction of ~0.24 (24% of peak DRAM bandwidth). Final file: `/workspace/problems/03_paged_attention/solution.py`.

1	"""Naive PyTorch paged-attention decode reference (correctness oracle, not SOTA).
2	
3	Single-query decode: each batch element has a query of shape (num_heads, head_dim)
4	and attends over a KV cache of `seq_len[b]` tokens stored as fixed-size pages in
5	a global pool. Pages for batch element b are listed in `block_table[b]`.
6	
7	The reference performs the slow path:
8	  1. Gather pages -> contiguous (seq_len, num_kv_heads, head_dim) per batch element.
9	  2. Repeat KV heads for grouped-query (broadcast num_kv_heads -> num_heads).
10	  3. Manual softmax(QK^T / sqrt(d)) @ V in fp32, cast back to bf16.
11	
12	This avoids torch.nn.functional.scaled_dot_product_attention (which is on the
13	forbidden list) so the agent cannot dispatch through SDPA either.
14	"""
15	import math
16	
17	import torch
18	import torch.nn as nn
19	
20	OP_TYPE = "attention"
21	SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
22	HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]
23	
24	
25	# --- Shape knobs (overridden by check.py / benchmark.py from shapes.py) ----
26	BATCH = 8
27	NUM_HEADS = 32
28	NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
29	HEAD_DIM = 128
30	SEQ_LEN = 1024
31	PAGE_SIZE = 16
32	
33	
34	class Model(nn.Module):
35	    """Single-query paged attention decode.
36	
37	    Forward inputs (all on device):
38	      query:       (batch, num_heads, head_dim)               bf16
39	      kv_cache:    (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2)
40	                   Layout: last dim packs [K | V] so a single gather pulls both.
4

1	"""SOTA reference for paged-attention decode.
2	
3	Tries, in order:
4	  1. FlashInfer's BatchDecodeWithPagedKVCacheWrapper (preferred -- portable,
5	     supports SM120, GQA, arbitrary head_dim).
6	  2. vLLM's paged_attention_v2 CUDA op (requires its KV-cache layout, more
7	     finicky; we adapt the layout on the fly when possible).
8	
9	If neither is importable, is_available() returns False and the benchmark just
10	reports eager + compiled + solution.
11	
12	Agents are FORBIDDEN from importing these in solution.py (see problem.yaml).
13	This file is only for the benchmark's reference line.
14	"""
15	from __future__ import annotations
16	
17	import torch
18	
19	
20	def _try_flashinfer(
21	    query: torch.Tensor,
22	    kv_cache: torch.Tensor,
23	    block_table: torch.Tensor,
24	    seq_lens: torch.Tensor,
25	    num_kv_heads: int,
26	    head_dim: int,

28	) -> torch.Tensor | None:

30	        import flashinfer  # noqa: F401
31	        from flashinfer.decode import BatchDecodeWithPagedKVCacheWrapper
32	    except Exception:
33	        return None

36	    # FlashInfer expects K and V as separate (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim) tensors.
37	    # Our reference packs [K|V] on the last dim -- split here.
38	    k_cache = kv_cache[..., :D].contiguous()
39	    v_cache = kv_cache[..., D:].contiguous()
40	
41	    workspace = torch.empty(128 * 1024 * 1024, dtype=torch.uint8, device=query.device)

1	name: 03_paged_attention
2	display_name: "Paged Attention Decode"
3	precision: bf16
4	regime: memory  # decode is bandwidth-bound (KV cache streamed once per token)
5	
6	# Effective FLOPs per call: QK^T + softmax*V across all batches/heads/seq.
7	# Sum-formula evaluated per-shape; the benchmark substitutes batch/num_heads/etc.
8	# 2 * B * H * L * D for QK^T plus 2 * B * H * L * D for AV  =>  4 * B * H * L * D
9	flops_formula: "4 * batch * num_heads * seq_len * head_dim"
10	
11	# Bytes moved (the real bottleneck): the KV cache must be streamed end-to-end.
12	#   K and V each:  batch * seq_len * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 bytes (bf16)
13	#   Q: batch * num_heads * head_dim * 2  (negligible vs KV)
14	#   Out: same as Q
15	# So total ~ 2 * (B * L * Hkv * D * 2) + small.
16	bytes_formula: "2 * batch * seq_len * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 + batch * num_heads * head_dim * 2 * 2"
17	
18	hardware: [RTX_PRO_6000]
19	peak_tflops_key: bf16          # informational; regime=memory uses bandwidth
20	peak_bandwidth_key: dram        # 1.8 TB/s GDDR7 on RTX PRO 6000 Blackwell
21	
22	tolerance:
23	  bfloat16: 0.02
24	  float16: 0.02
25	
26	# Forbidden ops -- using any of these in solution.py fails correctness post-hoc.
27	# vllm.attention / flashinfer.batch_decode_with_paged_kv_cache: dispatching to
28	# the SOTA library is the trivial cheat. SDPA is also banned because the agent
29	# could gather pages then call SDPA and inherit FlashAttention "for free".
30	forbidden:
31	  - "vllm.attenti

Need kernel for single-query decode with paged KV. Triton 3.6 has new warp scheduling etc. Need support block tables, arbitrary seq_lens, page_size 16, head_dim 64/128, GQA. A single Triton kernel can process all (batch, heads) heads. Need high bandwidth. Decode memory-bound: load each KV token once per query head. We can have each head query loop over pages/tokens, compute dot and weighted sum, fused. This is simplest and bandwidth-optimal (loads each KV token exactly once per query head). Compute not huge. We need efficient vectorized loads from kv_cache. The layout is (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim*2). block_table maps physical block index. Use block ptr with block_table to load per token. Triton kernel design options: 1. One thread block per head per batch, compute attention over seq_len sequentially. BLOCK_SIZE (tokens per iteration) maybe 64 or 128 tokens; load chunks, compute QK, softmax online, accumulate. Use shared memory for Q vector, V accum. For D=128, a block has 4 warps? Need enough warps to hide memory latency. Each head block loads KV chunk across seq. Need coordinate with page_size 16. Use BLOCK_N tokens per iteration. Block table page indices loaded, get physical block ids. Each token within page. Alternatively, use split-KV across sequence within a head (warps compute partial softmax then combine). VLLM paged attention v2 uses this to improve occupancy. But simpler one block per head may be okay for seq_len <=4096, batch*heads up to 32*32=1024 blocks. On Blackwell 128 SMs, enough. But occupancy low if each block uses too many warps. For 1024 blocks, that's okay. For B=4,H=64 => 256 blocks; B=32,H=32 => 1024 blocks. With each block one warp? Need enough registers. Let's see. Simpler: one warp per head? head_dim 128, load Q vector per warp, then iterate tokens. Need each warp can do vectorized loads. But one warp has limited registers; we need store V accum of D floats in registers. D up to 128 floats per warp = ~512 bytes per warp, fine. Q floats 128, 512 bytes. Softmax max, sum floats. Need loading K/V per token from HBM in registers or shared memory. Each token: load K of D bf16 (256 bytes) and V (256 bytes) per head (not per kv head? because GQA). Wait for GQA, each KV head shared by G query heads. If one block per query head, each loads same KV tokens multiple times (G times), which is inefficient. But problem's bytes_formula counts only one stream of KV per batch, but actual compute loads each KV per query head if block per head. GQA ratio up to 8 (H=64,Hkv=8 => G=8). That would load KV 8x, hurting bandwidth. For memory-bound decode, GQA should be exploited: each KV head processed once per group, sharing KV loads. We should design kernel at granularity of KV head and group: each block handles one batch element and one KV head, computing all G query heads simultaneously. This loads K/V once per token and computes G dot products. Output head_dim*G. Good. Need block_table per batch. So grid (B, Hkv) blocks. Each block computes G = H/Hkv query heads. For D=128, G up to 8. Block can have multiple warps to compute G outputs. Each warp can handle one query head? Then load K/V token shared among warps? We can load K and V into shared memory per token (or per chunk of tokens) and compute G dots in parallel. For efficiency, process tokens in chunks of BLOCK_N (e.g., 16 or 32) tokens, load K and V for chunk into SMEM, then compute G query dots across warps. But shared memory size: BLOCK_N * D * 2 (K+V) * 2 bytes = for BLOCK_N=32,D=128 => 32*128*2*2=16KB. For BLOCK_N=64 =>32KB. D=64 => half. Plus Q vectors G*D floats maybe 8*128*4=4KB. SMEM fine. Need to handle page_table indexing: tokens in chunk may span pages of size 16. Since BLOCK_N can be 16 (page size) for simple one page per chunk. Use BLOCK_N=16 to align with pages. Then each chunk corresponds to one physical page for a given batch and kv head (since block_table per batch lists pages; each page contains all kv heads, page_size tokens). Within page, token offset 0..15. So we can load one page per block per kv head per batch. However seq_len may not be multiple of page_size; tail predicated. If BLOCK_N=16, number of chunks = num_pages per sequence. For each chunk: use block_table[b, page_idx] physical block id. Load K and V for that page: shape (page_size, head_dim) for that kv head. Since kv_cache last dim packs K|V: offset for head kv: start = kv_head*D*2; k = start..start+D, v=start+D..start+2D. Need gather only one physical block per iteration. Triton block pointer with block_shape=(page_size, D) at offset [physical_block, 0, kv_head, k_offset] maybe. But packed last dim contiguous, can split into two pointers. Alternatively, BLOCK_N=32 would load two pages and gather two physical blocks per iteration, more complex. Use BLOCK_N=16 to match page_size. Then grid x = B, y = Hkv, z = num_pages? Or each block loops over pages. Looping per page with (B, Hkv) blocks and inner loop over pages is fine. For seq_len up to 4096, pages per seq up to 256, each block loops 256 iterations. Blocks count = B*Hkv, e.g., 4*8=32 blocks for longest context, occupancy low but enough? 32 blocks only; each block heavy loop. For B=32,Hkv=8 => 256 blocks with 64-128 pages each. That's okay. For B=8,Hkv=8 =>64 blocks with 64 pages. Occupancy maybe low but still. Could set grid = (B, Hkv, num_pages_max) to parallel pages and then reduce per seq? But then need reduction across pages with softmax (more complex). Loop likely fine for memory-bound. To improve occupancy for small B*Hkv, we could split head_dim or other. However Triton kernel with block per (b,kv_head) loops over pages. Need handle each chunk size=16; tail page may have fewer tokens than page_size. We can predicate with token mask based on seq_len. Within a page, valid tokens = min(PAGE_SIZE, seq_len - page_idx*PAGE_SIZE). Use mask when loading K/V and computing. Need store Q vectors in SMEM or registers? G query heads per block. We can load Q for group into shared memory: shape (G, D) bf16. Each warp can hold one q? Simpler: load Q into shared memory, each thread computes across D for all G? Let's think. Per page chunk of K,V loaded into shared memory of shape (BLOCK_N, D) for K and V (bf16). Then each thread computes partial? Since D=128 and BLOCK_N=16, total elements per K chunk 2048. If we use e.g. 4 warps per block (128 threads), each thread could process one token? We need compute G scores per token and output D accum. Approach: Option A: Assign each warp to one query head (G <= 8 -> up to 8 warps). Warp computes its q (D floats regs), then loops tokens in SMEM K chunk to compute scores (16 floats), stores scores in SMEM/shared; then softmax across tokens (16) within warp; then loads V chunk and accumulates weighted sum. This is natural. K and V loaded into SMEM once and shared by all warps. Each warp reads K from SMEM for its score. Shared memory broadcast. For D=128, K chunk 16x128=2048 bf16=4KB, V chunk=4KB, total 8KB; Q per warp in registers. Number of warps = G (up to 8). Block threads = G*32 up to 256. That's okay. For G=4 (D=64 case) use 4 warps. We can treat q as (1,D), K_chunk as (BLOCK_N,D), want scores (1,BLOCK_N) = q @ K_chunk.T. Triton has tl.trans. tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k_chunk)) => (1,D) @ (D,BLOCK_N) => (1,BLOCK_N). Good. Need block-level dot with K in SMEM. But tl.dot with small BLOCK_N=16 and D=128 maybe uses tensor cores; could be okay. However to use tl.dot, data must be in block pointers with certain dimensions. Simpler to manually compute dot per token using vectorized loads. Given decode is memory-bound, dot overhead okay. But Triton tl.dot may be more efficient and use tensor cores. But manual dot easier for masking and GQA. Potential issue: The kernel needs to be correctness-tolerant 0.02; softmax numerical stability matters. Use online softmax in fp32: for each token chunk, compute q*k*scale, subtract running max, exponentiate, update sum and accum. Algorithm per block (b, kv_head): - G = NUM_HEADS // NUM_KV_HEADS - tid, wid, lane - Load Q for group into registers or SMEM. Since each warp handles one q head, load q for warp_id head. q: shape (D,) bf16 -> convert to fp32. Implementation details for Triton kernel with block per (b,hkv), sequential G: ``` @triton.jit def paged_decode_kernel( q_ptr, kv_ptr, block_table_ptr, seq_lens_ptr, out_ptr, stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_qd, stride_kv_n, stride_kv_t, stride_kv_h, stride_kv_d, stride_bt_b, stride_bt_p, stride_ob, stride_oh, stride_od, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr, PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr, SCALE: tl.constexpr ): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1) G = NUM_HEADS // NUM_KV_HEADS seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens_ptr + pid_b) num_pages = tl.cdiv(seq_len, PAGE_SIZE) # initialize per head accumulators outside? Since sequential over heads, inside g loop. for g in range(G): # compute h = pid_hkv*G + g q_ptrs = q_ptr + pid_b*stride_qb + (pid_hkv*G + g)*stride_qh + tl.arange(0, HEAD_DIM)*stride_qd q = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=tl.arange(0,HEAD_DIM)<HEAD_DIM, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) m = float('-inf') l = 0.0 acc = tl.zeros((HEAD_DIM,), dtype=tl.float32) for p in range(num_pages): physical_block = tl.load(block_table_ptr + pid_b*stride_bt_b + p*stride_bt_p) token_offset = p*PAGE_SIZE valid = tl.minimum(PAGE_SIZE, seq_len - token_offset) # K pointer base for page offs_t = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE) offs_d = tl.arange(0, HEAD_DIM) kv_base = kv_ptr + physical_block*stride_kv_n + pid_hkv*stride_kv_h k_ptrs = kv_base + (offs_t[:,None]*stride_kv_t + offs_d[None,:]) k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=(offs_t[:,None] < valid) & (offs_d[None,:] < HEAD_DIM), other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # V pointer base with +HEAD_DIM offset v_ptrs = kv_base + HEAD_DIM*stride_kv_d + (offs_t[:,None]*stride_kv_t + offs_d[None,:]) v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=(offs_t[:,None] < valid) & (offs_d[None,:] < HEAD_DIM), other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # scores scores = tl.sum(q[None,:] * k, axis=1) * SCALE scores = tl.where(offs_t < valid, scores, float('-inf')) # online softmax m_new = tl.maximum(m, tl.max(scores, axis=0)) exp_scale = tl.exp(m - m_new) exp_scores = tl.exp(scores - m_new) acc = acc * exp_scale + tl.sum(exp_scores[:,None] * v, axis=0) l = l * exp_scale + tl.sum(exp_scores, axis=0) m = m_new out = acc / l out_ptrs = out_ptr + pid_b*stride_ob + (pid_hkv*G + g)*stride_oh + tl.arange(0,HEAD_DIM)*stride_od tl.store(out_ptrs, out.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=tl.arange(0,HEAD_DIM)<HEAD_DIM) ``` Issues: - `q[None,:] * k` broadcasting? q shape (HEAD_DIM,), k shape (PAGE_SIZE,HEAD_DIM); broadcast q across rows gives (PAGE_SIZE,HEAD_DIM). tl.sum axis=1 gives (PAGE_SIZE). Good. - m is scalar; but Triton expects tensors. Using Python float might work in tl.maximum? Need use `tl.full((), float('-inf'), dtype=tl.float32)`. We can initialize `m = tl.full((1,), float('-inf'), dtype=tl.float32)`. Then tl.maximum(m, tl.max(scores, axis=0)[None]) maybe shapes. Need be careful. We can treat as 0-d tensor. `m = tl.full((), float('-inf'), tl.float32)`. Then `m_new = tl.maximum(m, tl.max(scores))`. But `scores` shape (PAGE_SIZE). `tl.max(scores, axis=0)` returns scalar? Might be 0-d. `tl.maximum` of 0-d and 0-d ok. `exp_scale = tl.exp(m - m_new)` scalar. `acc * exp_scale` broadcasts. `tl.sum(exp_scores[:,None]*v, axis=0)` returns (HEAD_DIM). Good. - For first iteration, if all scores -inf? Not possible. - Division by l when l=0? not. - We need `m` across pages. At the end, acc already normalized? Wait online algorithm formula: We maintain m (max), l (sum of exp relative to current max), acc (weighted sum relative to current max). After processing chunk, update: new_m = max(m, m_chunk) alpha = exp(m - new_m) new_l = l*alpha + sum(exp(s - new_m)) new_acc = acc*alpha + sum(exp(s - new_m)*v) At end output = acc / l. This is correct (acc is sum exp(s-m_current)*v, l is sum exp(s-m_current)). Yes. - For chunk where m_new equals m_chunk > m, alpha=exp(old_m - new_m), exp_scores relative to new_m. +"""Paged attention decode kernel implemented in Triton.
+
+Conforms to the same Model/get_inputs/get_init_inputs interface as reference.py.
+"""
+import math
+from typing import List
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+
+OP_TYPE = "attention"
+SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
+HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]
+
+BATCH = 8
+NUM_HEADS = 32
+NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
+HEAD_DIM = 128
+SEQ_LEN = 1024
+PAGE_SIZE = 16
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def paged_decode_kernel(
+    q_ptr,
+    kv_ptr,
+    block_table_ptr,
+    seq_lens_ptr,
+    out_ptr,
+    stride_qb,
+    stride_qh,
+    stride_qd,
+    stride_kvn,
+    stride_kvt,
+    stride_kvh,
+    stride_kvd,
+    stride_bt_b,
+    stride_bt_p,
+    stride_ob,
+    stride_oh,
+    stride_od,
+    SCALE: tl.constexpr,
+    PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
+    G: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    """One CUDA block per (batch, kv_head). Computes all G query heads."""
+    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
+    pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1)
+
+    seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens_ptr + pid_b)
+    num_pages = tl.cdiv(seq_len, PAGE_SIZE)
+
+    # Load all query heads belonging to this KV group into a (G, D) tensor.
+    offs_d = tl.arange(0, HEAD_DIM)
+    qs = tl.zeros((G, HEAD_DIM), dtype=tl.float32)
+    base_q = q_ptr + pid_b * stride_qb + pid_hkv * G * stride_qh
+    for g in tl.static_range(G):
+        q_ptrs = base_q + g * stride_qh + offs_d * stride_qd
+        qs = tl.sum(
+            qs + tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=offs_d < HEAD_DIM, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)[None, :],
+            axis=0,
+        )  # no-op sum just to scatter; actually this is wrong.
+
+
+class Model(nn.Module):
+    def __init__(
+        self,
+        batch: int,
+        num_heads: int,
+        num_kv_heads: int,
+        head_dim: int,
+        seq_len: int,
+        page_size: int,
+    ):
+        super().__init__()
+        assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0
+        self.batch = batch
+        self.num_heads = num_heads
+        self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads
+        self.head_dim = head_dim
+        self.seq_len = seq_len
+        self.page_size = page_size
+        self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads
+        self.scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)
+        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False)
+
+    def forward(
+        self,
+        query: torch.Tensor,
+        kv_cache: torch.Tensor,
+        block_table: torch.Tensor,
+        seq_lens: torch.Tensor,
+    ) -> torch.Tensor:
+        B, H, D = query.shape
+        Hkv = self.num_kv_heads
+        G = self.group_size
+        P = self.page_size
+
+        out = torch.empty(B, H, D, dtype=query.dtype, device=query.device)
+
+        grid = (B, Hkv)
+        paged_decode_kernel[grid](
+            query,
+            kv_cache,
+            block_table,
+            seq_lens,
+            out,
+            query.stride(0),
+            query.stride(1),
+            query.stride(2),
+            kv_cache.stride(0),
+            kv_cache.stride(1),
+            kv_cache.stride(2),
+            kv_cache.stride(3),
+            block_table.stride(0),
+            block_table.stride(1),
+            out.stride(0),
+            out.stride(1),
+            out.stride(2),
+            SCALE=self.scale,
+            PAGE_SIZE=P,
+            HEAD_DIM=D,
+            G=G,
+            num_warps=4,
+        )
+        return out
+
+
+def get_inputs():
+    B = BATCH
+    H = NUM_HEADS
+    Hkv = NUM_KV_HEADS
+    D = HEAD_DIM
+    L = SEQ_LEN
+    P = PAGE_SIZE
+
+    pages_per_seq = (L + P - 1) // P
+    total_pages = max(B * pages_per_seq + 8, 64)
+
+    query = torch.randn(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
+    kv_cache = torch.randn(total_pages, P, Hkv, 2 * D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
+
+    perm = torch.randperm(total_pages)[: B * pages_per_seq].reshape(B, pages_per_seq).int()
+    block_table = perm.contiguous()
+    seq_lens = torch.full((B,), L, dtype=torch.int32)
+
+    return [query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens]
+
+
+def get_init_inputs():
+    return [BATCH, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM, SEQ_LEN, PAGE_SIZE]

+            weighted = tl.dot(exp_scores[None, :], v)[0, :]
+
+            new_acc = accs[g, :] * exp_scale + weighted
+            new_l = ls[g] * exp_scale + tl.sum(exp_scores, axis=0)
+
+            mask_g = offs_g1 == g
+            mask_g2 = mask_g[:, None]
+            accs = tl.where(mask_g2, new_acc[None, :], accs)
+            ls = tl.where(mask_g, new_l, ls)
+            ms = tl.where(mask_g, m_new, ms)
+
+    out_ptrs = (
+        out_ptr
+        + pid_b * stride_ob
+        + (pid_hkv * G + offs_g) * stride_oh
+        + offs_d[None, :] * stride_od
+    )
+    tl.store(
+        out_ptrs,
+        (accs / ls[:, None]).to(tl.bfloat16),
+        mask=offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM,
+    )

import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(x_ptr, y_ptr, HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr):
    offs_d = tl.arange(0, HEAD_DIM)
    x = tl.load(x_ptr + offs_d).to(tl.float32)  # (HEAD_DIM,)
    idx = tl.full((1, HEAD_DIM), 0, dtype=tl.int32)
    row = tl.gather(x[None,:], idx, axis=0)  # gather from (1,HEAD_DIM)
    tl.store(y_ptr + offs_d, row[0,:])

a = torch.randn(1,128,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device='cuda')
b = torch.empty(128,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device='cuda')
test_kernel[(1,)](a,b,HEAD_DIM=128)
print('ok', (b-a[0]).abs().max())

import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(x_ptr, y_ptr, N: tl.constexpr):
    # try tuple comprehension
    t = (tl.load(x_ptr + i) for i in range(N))
    s = 0.0
    for i in tl.static_range(N):

    tl.store(y_ptr, s)

import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(x_ptr, y_ptr, N: tl.constexpr):
    a0 = tl.zeros((), dtype=tl.float32)
    a1 = tl.zeros((), dtype=tl.float32)
    a2 = tl.zeros((), dtype=tl.float32)

import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(x_ptr, y_ptr, N: tl.constexpr):
    offs = tl.arange(0, N)
    a = tl.load(x_ptr + offs)  # (N,)
    b = a[None, :]  # (1,N)
    c = tl.reshape(b, (N,))
    tl.store(y_ptr + offs, c)

a = torch.randn(16,dtype=torch.float32,device='cuda')
b = torch.empty(16,dtype=torch.float32,device='cuda')
test_kernel[(1,)](a,b,N=16)
print('ok', (a-b).abs().max())

cat > /tmp/test_sumsel.py <<'EOF'
import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(x_ptr, y_ptr, G: tl.constexpr, D: tl.constexpr):
    offs_d = tl.arange(0, D)
    offs_g = tl.arange(0, G)[:,None]
    x = tl.load(x_ptr + offs_g * D + offs_d[None,:])  # (G,D)
    g = 1
    mask = (tl.arange(0, G) == g)[:,None]
    row = tl.sum(x * mask, axis=0)
    tl.store(y_ptr + offs_d, row)

a = torch.arange(8*64,dtype=torch.float32,device='cuda').reshape(8,64)
b = torch.empty(64,dtype=torch.float32,device='cuda')
test_kernel[(1,)](a,b,G=8,D=64)
print('ok', (b - a[1]).abs().max())
EOF

import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(x_ptr, y_ptr):
    a = tl.load(x_ptr)
    b = tl.exp(a)
    tl.store(y_ptr, b)

a = torch.tensor(float('-inf'),dtype=torch.float32,device='cuda')
b = torch.empty(1,dtype=torch.float32,device='cuda')
test_kernel[(1,)](a,b)

import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(x_ptr, y_ptr, N: tl.constexpr):
    offs = tl.arange(0, N)
    x = tl.load(x_ptr + offs)
    m = tl.max(x, axis=0)
    tl.store(y_ptr, m)

a = torch.tensor([-float('inf'), -1.0, -2.0],dtype=torch.float32,device='cuda')

import sys, torch
sys.path.insert(0,'/workspace/problems/03_paged_attention')
import reference, solution

shape = {'batch':8,'num_heads':32,'num_kv_heads':8,'head_dim':128,'seq_len':1024,'page_size':16}
for mod in [reference, solution]:
    mod.BATCH=shape['batch']; mod.NUM_HEADS=shape['num_heads']; mod.NUM_KV_HEADS=shape['num_kv_heads']; mod.HEAD_DIM=shape['head_dim']; mod.SEQ_LEN=shape['seq_len']; mod.PAGE_SIZE=shape['page_size']

torch.manual_seed(42)
inputs = [t.cuda() for t in reference.get_inputs()]
ref = reference.Model(*reference.get_init_inputs()).cuda().eval()
sol = solution.Model(*solution.get_init_inputs()).cuda().eval()
with torch.no_grad():
    ref_out = ref(*inputs)
    sol_out = sol(*inputs)
print('ref nan', ref_out.isnan().any().item(), 'sol nan', sol_out.isnan().any().item())
print('sol max', sol_out.abs().max().item(), 'min', sol_out.min().item(), 'max ref', ref_out.abs().max().item())
print('diff finite', (sol_out - ref_out).abs()[~sol_out.isnan()].max().item())
# print first nan location
if sol_out.isnan().any():
    idx = torch.where(sol_out.isnan())
    print('nan loc', idx[0][0].item(), idx[1][0].item(), idx[2][0].item())

String: @triton.jit
def paged_decode_kernel(
    q_ptr,
    kv_ptr,
    block_table_ptr,
    seq_lens_ptr,
    out_ptr,
    stride_qb,
    stride_qh,
    stride_qd,
    stride_kvn,
    stride_kvt,
    stride_kvh,
    stride_kvd,
    stride_bt_b,
    stride_bt_p,
    stride_ob,
    stride_oh,
    stride_od,
    SCALE: tl.constexpr,
    PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
    G: tl.constexpr,
):
    """One CUDA block per (batch, kv_head). Computes all G query heads."""
    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
    pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1)

    seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens_ptr + pid_b)
    num_pages = tl.cdiv(seq_len, PAGE_SIZE)

    offs_d = tl.arange(0, HEAD_DIM)
    offs_g = tl.arange(0, G)[:, None]

    # Load the G query heads for this KV group: (G, HEAD_DIM).
    q_ptrs = (
        q_ptr
        + pid_b * stride_qb
        + (pid_hkv * G + offs_g) * stride_qh
        + offs_d[None, :] * stride_qd
    )
    qs = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)

    ms = tl.full((G,), float("-inf"), dtype=tl.float32)
    ls = tl.zeros((G,), dtype=tl.float32)
    accs = tl.zeros((G, HEAD_DIM), dtype=tl.float32)

    offs_t = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)
    for p in range(num_pages):
        physical_block = tl.load(
            block_table_ptr + pid_b * stride_bt_b + p * stride_bt_p
        ).to(tl.int64)
        token_offset = p * PAGE_SIZE
        valid = tl.minimum(PAGE_SIZE, seq_len - token_off

cat(input, other, can_reorder=False, _semantic=None)
    Concatenate the given blocks
    
    :param input: The first input tensor.
    :type input: Tensor
    :param other: The second input tensor.
    :type other: Tensor
    :param reorder: Compiler hint. If true, the compiler is

import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(x_ptr, y_ptr, N: tl.constexpr):
    offs = tl.arange(0, N)
    a = tl.load(x_ptr + offs)  # (N,)
    b = tl.load(x_ptr + N + offs)
    c = tl.cat(a, b)
    tl.store(y_ptr + tl.arange(0, 2*N), c)

N=4
x = torch.arange(8,dtype=torch.float32,device='cuda')
y = torch.empty(8,dtype=torch.float32,device='cuda')
test_kernel[(1,)](x,y,N=N)
print('y=', y)
EOF

+@triton.jit
+def combine_kernel(
+    part_out_ptr,
+    part_m_ptr,
+    part_l_ptr,
+    out_ptr,
+    stride_pob,
+    stride_poh,
+    stride_pos,
+    stride_pod,
+    stride_pmb,
+    stride_pmh,
+    stride_pms,
+    stride_ob,
+    stride_oh,
+    stride_od,
+    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
+    NUM_SPLITS: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    """Combine partial attention results across splits."""
+    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
+    pid_h = tl.program_id(1)
+
+    offs_d = tl.arange(0, HEAD_DIM)
+
+    M = tl.full((), float("-inf"), dtype=tl.float32)
+    denom = tl.zeros((), dtype=tl.float32)
+    acc = tl.zeros((HEAD_DIM,), dtype=tl.float32)
+
+    base_out = part_out_ptr + pid_b * stride_pob + pid_h * stride_poh
+    base_m = part_m_ptr + pid_b * stride_pmb + pid_h * stride_pmh
+    base_l = part_l_ptr + pid_b * stride_pmb + pid_h * stride_pmh
+
+    for s in tl.static_range(NUM_SPLITS):
+        m_s = tl.load(base_m + s * stride_pms)
+        l_s = tl.load(base_l + s * stride_pms)
+        acc_s = tl.load(base_out + s * stride_pos + offs_d * stride_pod, mask=offs_d < HEAD_DIM, other=0.0)
+
+        M_new = tl.maximum(M, m_s)
+        scale_global = tl.exp(M - M_new)
+        scale_s = tl.exp(m_s - M_new)
+
+        acc = acc * scale_global + acc_s * scale_s
+        denom = denom * scale_global + l_s * scale_s
+        M = M_new
+
+    out_ptrs = out_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob + pid_h * stride_oh + offs_d * stride_od
     tl.store(

I attempted to pass `out` as part_out but kernel writes accs to out as if shape (B,H,1,D) but out is (B,H,D); strides 0 for split dims; it will write at h offset with accs vector, ignoring split. That would actually write accs directly to out[b,h,:] if stride_pos=0, stride_pod=1. But part_m/l writes to out with stride 0, corrupting output. So single-split path is wrong. Better always use split path, with num_splits at least 1, allocate part_out (B,H,1,D), combine. That adds combine overhead but small. Or use original output-writing kernel for num_splits=1. --- a//workspace/problems/03_paged_attention/solution.py
+++ b//workspace/problems/03_paged_attention/solution.py
@@ -20,6 +20,113 @@
 HEAD_DIM = 128
 SEQ_LEN = 1024
 PAGE_SIZE = 16
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def paged_decode_kernel(
+    q_ptr,
+    kv_ptr,
+    block_table_ptr,
+    seq_lens_ptr,
+    out_ptr,
+    stride_qb,
+    stride_qh,
+    stride_qd,
+    stride_kvn,
+    stride_kvt,
+    stride_kvh,
+    stride_kvd,
+    stride_bt_b,
+    stride_bt_p,
+    stride_ob,
+    stride_oh,
+    stride_od,
+    SCALE: tl.constexpr,
+    PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
+    G: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    """One CUDA block per (batch, kv_head). Computes all G query heads."""
+    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
+    pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1)
+
+    seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens_ptr + pid_b)
+    num_pages = tl.cdiv(seq_len, PAGE_SIZE)
+
+    offs_d = tl.arange(0, HEAD_DIM)
+    offs_t = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)
+    offs_g = tl.arange(0, G)[:, None]
+
+    # Load the G query heads for this KV group: (G, HEAD_DIM).
+    q_ptrs = (
+        q_ptr
+        + pid_b * stride_qb
+        + (pid_hkv * G + offs_g) * stride_qh
+        + offs_d[None, :] * stride_qd
+    )
+    qs = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)
+
+    ms = tl.full((G,), float("-inf"), dtype=tl.float32)
+    ls = tl.zeros((G,), dtype=tl.float32)
+    accs = tl.zeros((G, HEAD_DIM), dtype=tl.float32)
+
+    for p in range(num_pages):
+        physical_block = tl.load(
+            block_table_ptr + pid_b * stride_bt_b + p * stride_bt_p
+        ).to(tl.int64)
+        token_offset = p * PAGE_SIZE
+        valid = tl.minimum(PAGE_SIZE, seq_len - token_offset)
+
+        kv_base = kv_ptr + physical_block * stride_kvn + pid_hkv * stride_kvh
+        k_ptrs = kv_base + (offs_t[:, None] * stride_kvt + offs_d[None, :] * stride_kvd)
+        k = tl.load(
+            k_ptrs,
+            mask=(offs_t[:, None] < valid) & (offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM),
+            other=0.0,
+        ).to(tl.float32)
+        v_ptrs = kv_base + HEAD_DIM * stride_kvd + (
+            offs_t[:, None] * stride_kvt + offs_d[None, :] * stride_kvd
+        )
+        v = tl.load(
+            v_ptrs,
+            mask=(offs_t[:, None] < valid) & (offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM),
+            other=0.0,
+        ).to(tl.float32)
+
+        for g in tl.static_range(G):
+            mask_g = tl.arange(0, G) == g
+            mask_g2 = mask_g[:, None]
+            q = tl.sum(tl.where(mask_g2, qs, 0.0), axis=0)
+            acc_cur = tl.sum(tl.where(mask_g2, accs, 0.0), axis=0)
+            m_cur = tl.sum(tl.where(mask_g, ms, 0.0), axis=0)
+            l_cur = tl.sum(tl.where(mask_g, ls, 0.0), axis=0)
+
+            scores = tl.reshape(tl.dot(q[None, :], tl.trans(k)), (PAGE_SIZE,)) * SCALE
+            scores = tl.where(offs_t < valid, scores, float("-inf"))
+
+            m_new = tl.maximum(m_cur, tl.max(scores, axis=0))
+            exp_scale = tl.exp(m_cur - m_new)
+            exp_scores = tl.exp(scores - m_new)
+            weighted = tl.reshape(tl.dot(exp_scores[None, :], v), (HEAD_DIM,))
+
+            new_acc = acc_cur * exp_scale + weighted
+            new_l = l_cur * exp_scale + tl.sum(exp_scores, axis=0)
+
+            accs = tl.where(mask_g2, new_acc[None, :], accs)
+            ls = tl.where(mask_g, new_l, ls)
+            ms = tl.where(mask_g, m_new, ms)
+
+    out_ptrs = (
+        out_ptr
+        + pid_b * stride_ob
+        + (pid_hkv * G + offs_g) * stride_oh
+        + offs_d[None, :] * stride_od
+    )
+    tl.store(
+        out_ptrs,
+        (accs / ls[:, None]).to(tl.bfloat16),
+        mask=offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM,
+    )

assistant
Implemented the paged-attention decode kernel in `solution.py`. What it does: - Custom Triton kernel (no forbidden ops / libraries). - One CUDA block per `(batch, kv_head)` so the KV cache is streamed only once per KV head; each block computes all GQA query heads in the group. - Fused online softmax in fp32, with predicated masking for non-power-of-two sequence lengths. - Splits the page sequence into partitions when batch × kv-head is small, then combines partial softmax states in a second small kernel. This boosts occupancy on the long-context / small-batch shapes. - Uses `tl.dot` for the QK and PV reductions on each page tile. Verification: - `python check.py` → **PASS** across all five shapes and seeds. - `python benchmark.py` → **RESULT: OK** with a geometric-mean peak fraction of ~0.24 (24% of peak DRAM bandwidth). Final file: `/workspace/problems/03_paged_attention/solution.py`.
